<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2013_Stanley_Cup_Final" class="mw-redirect" title="2013 Stanley Cup Final">Final</a>, they faced the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Blackhawks" title="Chicago Blackhawks">Chicago Blackhawks</a>, another <a href="/wiki/Original_Six" title="Original Six">Original Six</a> team. The Bruins fell in six games, with three going into overtime, including an epic Game 1 in which a third overtime period was needed before it was settled. The only game Boston lost by more than one goal was Game 5 in which Chicago scored on an empty net in the last 17 seconds.</p>
<p>The 2013 Stanley Cup run by the Bruins was one that further united the New England region that had been rocked by tragedies, such as the Boston Marathon bombing and the <a href="/wiki/Sandy_Hook_Elementary_School_shooting" title="Sandy Hook Elementary School shooting">Sandy Hook Elementary School shooting</a>. Coach <a href="/wiki/Claude_Julien_(ice_hockey)" title="Claude Julien (ice hockey)">Claude Julien</a> said after the deciding Game 6, "You know, at the end of the day, I think that's what hurts the most is in the back of our minds, although we needed to focus on our team and doing what was going to be the best thing for our team to win a Stanley Cup, in the back of our minds we wanted to do it for those kind of reasons, the City of Boston, what Newtown has been through, that kind of stuff. It hit close to home, and the best way we felt we could try and cheer the area was to win a Stanley Cup. I think that's what's hard right now for the players. We had more reasons than just ourselves to win a Cup."</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2014.E2.80.93present">2014–present</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston_Bruins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2014–present">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_NHL_season" title="2013–14 NHL season">2013–14 season</a>, the Bruins won the <a href="/wiki/Presidents%27_Trophy" title="Presidents' Trophy">Presidents' Trophy</a> after finishing first in the newly formed <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Division_(NHL)" title="Atlantic Division (NHL)">Atlantic Division</a> with a record of 54–19–9 for 117 points. Their regular season success, however, would not translate into another Eastern Conference Finals appearance. Despite winning their first-round series against the <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Red_Wings" title="Detroit Red Wings">Detroit Red Wings</a>, the team fell to the Canadiens in seven games in the Eastern Conference Semifinals during the <a href="/wiki/2014_Stanley_Cup_playoffs" title="2014 Stanley Cup playoffs">2014 playoffs</a>.</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_NHL_season" title="2014–15 NHL season">2014–15 season</a>, the Bruins finished with a record of 41–27–14 for 96 points, missing out on the playoffs by just two points after the Pittsburgh Penguins and the Ottawa Senators clinched the final two playoff spots in the East. The Bruins therefore became only the third team to miss the playoffs after winning the Presidents' Trophy in the previous season. The 96 points they earned that season broke the record for the most points earned by a team that did not make the playoffs; the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Avalanche" title="Colorado Avalanche">Colorado Avalanche</a> finished with 95 points in the <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_NHL_season" title="2006–07 NHL season">2006–07</a>, which was the previous record.</p>
<p>On April 15, 2015, Chiarelli was fired by the Boston Bruins. On May 20, the Bruins named former player Don Sweeney as the team's new general manager for the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_NHL_season" title="2015–16 NHL season">2015–16 season</a>. One recent all-time franchise achievement the Bruins attained in the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Boston_Bruins_season" title="2015–16 Boston Bruins season">2015–16 season</a> is shared by only their greatest rival, the Canadiens – a total of 3,000 wins in the team's existence, achieved by the Bruins on January 8, 2016 in a 4–1 road victory against the <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Devils" title="New Jersey Devils">New Jersey Devils</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> The team was seen as a playoff contender throughout the regular season. However, a sub-.500 record on home ice and frequent road losses in the final two months of the regular season resulted in a three-way battle for the final playoff spot in the East. The Bruins had a chance to clinch the final playoff berth with a win over the Ottawa Senators on the second-to-last day of the season, but they lost the game. That loss, combined with a Flyers' win over the Penguins, knocked the Bruins out of playoff contention in favor of the Flyers. For the first time since the two seasons following the 2004–05 lockout, the Bruins did not qualify for the playoffs in two consecutive seasons.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ownership">Ownership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston_Bruins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Ownership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:JeremyJacobs.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/ea/JeremyJacobs.jpg/200px-JeremyJacobs.jpg" width="200" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/ea/JeremyJacobs.jpg/300px-JeremyJacobs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/ea/JeremyJacobs.jpg/400px-JeremyJacobs.jpg 2x" data-file-width="432" data-file-height="288" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:JeremyJacobs.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bruins legend and current president Cam Neely, and owner Jeremy Jacobs.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Team founder <a href="/wiki/Charles_Adams_(ice_hockey)" title="Charles Adams (ice hockey)">Charles Adams</a> owned the team until 1936, when he transferred his stock his son <a href="/wiki/Weston_Adams" title="Weston Adams">Weston Adams</a>, general manager and minority owner <a href="/wiki/Art_Ross" title="Art Ross">Art Ross</a> and minority owner Ralph Burkard.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Weston Adams remained majority owner until 1951, when the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Garden-Arena_Corporation" title="Boston Garden-Arena Corporation">Boston Garden-Arena Corporation</a> purchased controlling interest in the team.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Under the Garden-Arena Corporation's management, <a href="/wiki/Boston_Celtics" title="Boston Celtics">Boston Celtics</a> founder <a href="/wiki/Walter_A._Brown" title="Walter A. Brown">Walter A. Brown</a> ran the team from 1951 until his death in 1964. After Brown's death, Weston Adams returned to the role of team president. In 1969, he was succeeded by his son, <a href="/wiki/Weston_Adams,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Weston Adams, Jr.">Weston Adams, Jr.</a><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>On December 7, 1973, <a href="/wiki/Storer_Broadcasting" class="mw-redirect" title="Storer Broadcasting">Storer Broadcasting</a>, owner of <a href="/wiki/WSBK-TV" title="WSBK-TV">WSBK-TV</a>, and the Garden-Arena Corporation agreed to a merger which resulted in Storer acquiring a 100% interest in the Bruins. Adams remained as team president.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>In August 1975, Storer Broadcasting then sold the team to an ownership group headed by <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Jacobs" title="Jeremy Jacobs">Jeremy Jacobs</a>. Jacobs had to promise to keep Bobby Orr as a condition of the purchase.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrunt2006261.E2.80.93262_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrunt2006261.E2.80.93262-33">[33]</a></sup> The Bruins and Orr reached a verbal agreement with Jacobs during the summer of 1975, including a controversial agreement for Orr to take an 18.5% share of the Bruins after his playing days were over. The agreement was to be checked out as to whether it would be legal for tax reasons and whether or not the League would approve it. However, Orr's agent, the later-notorious <a href="/wiki/Alan_Eagleson" title="Alan Eagleson">Alan Eagleson</a>, rejected the deal.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrunt2006262_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrunt2006262-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>Jacobs represents the club on the NHL's Board of Governors, and serves on its Executive Committee, and he has chaired the Finance Committee. At the NHL Board of Governors meeting in June 2007, Jacobs was elected chairman of the Board, replacing the <a href="/wiki/Calgary_Flames" title="Calgary Flames">Calgary Flames</a>' <a href="/wiki/Harley_Hotchkiss" title="Harley Hotchkiss">Harley Hotchkiss</a>, who stepped down after 12 years in the position. Jacobs has frequently been listed by the <i><a href="/wiki/Sports_Business_Journal" class="mw-redirect" title="Sports Business Journal">Sports Business Journal</a></i> as one of the most influential people in sports in its annual poll<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> and by Hockey News.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> His company owns TD Garden and he is partners with <a href="/wiki/John_W._Henry" title="John W. Henry">John Henry</a>, owner of <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/New_England_Sports_Network" title="New England Sports Network">New England Sports Network</a> (NESN).</p>
<p>After taking over as owner in 1975, the Bruins have been competitive (making the playoffs for 29-straight seasons from <a href="/wiki/1967%E2%80%9368_NHL_season" title="1967–68 NHL season">1967–68</a> to <a href="/wiki/1995%E2%80%9396_NHL_season" title="1995–96 NHL season">1995–96</a>, 20 of which were with Jacobs as owner) but have won the Stanley Cup only once, in <a href="/wiki/2011_Stanley_Cup_Final" class="mw-redirect" title="2011 Stanley Cup Final">2011</a> and only in his 36th year as owner. Under previous ownerships, the Bruins had won the Stanley Cup five times. Under Jacobs, the Bruins have reached the Stanley Cup Final six times (twice against the Bruins' arch-rival Montreal Canadiens in <a href="/wiki/1977_Stanley_Cup_Final" class="mw-redirect" title="1977 Stanley Cup Final">1977</a> and <a href="/wiki/1978_Stanley_Cup_Final" class="mw-redirect" title="1978 Stanley Cup Final">1978</a>, twice against the <a href="/wiki/Edmonton_Oilers" title="Edmonton Oilers">Edmonton Oilers</a> in <a href="/wiki/1988_Stanley_Cup_Final" class="mw-redirect" title="1988 Stanley Cup Final">1988</a> and <a href="/wiki/1990_Stanley_Cup_Final" class="mw-redirect" title="1990 Stanley Cup Final">1990</a>, finally winning in 2011 against the <a href="/wiki/Vancouver_Canucks" title="Vancouver Canucks">Vancouver Canucks</a>, and losing in <a href="/wiki/2013_Stanley_Cup_Final" class="mw-redirect" title="2013 Stanley Cup Final">2013</a> to the Chicago Blackhawks). Jacobs' management of the team in the past earned him spots on <a href="/wiki/ESPN.com" title="ESPN.com">ESPN.com</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Page_2" class="mw-redirect" title="Page 2">Page 2</a>" polls of "The Worst Owners in Sports,"<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> and No.7 on their 2005 "Greediest Owners In sports" list.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Sports_Illustrated" title="Sports Illustrated">Sports Illustrated</a></i> has suggested longtime star defenseman Ray Bourque, who "often drawn the ire of the <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League_Players%27_Association" title="National Hockey League Players' Association">NHLPA</a> for his willingness to re-sign with Boston with minimal negotiations over the years" instead of setting the "watermark for defenseman salaries", requested and received a trade in 2000 since the team's "hardline and spendthrift ways" meant he would have to make the move to get his elusive Stanley Cup (Bourque holds the record for most games played before winning the Cup). <sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Prior to the <a href="/wiki/NHL_Collective_Bargaining_Agreement" title="NHL Collective Bargaining Agreement">NHL Collective Bargaining Agreement</a> signed in 2005, fans felt team management was not willing to spend to win the Stanley Cup.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since 2005, Jacobs' public image has improved as he invested in the team and rebuilding the front office to make the team more competitive. The Bruins were the second highest ranked team in the NHL in the 2008–09 season and were the top seeded team in the East. With a complete change in management, including now former General Manager <a href="/wiki/Peter_Chiarelli_(ice_hockey)" title="Peter Chiarelli (ice hockey)">Peter Chiarelli</a> — who lost his position with the Bruins on April 15, 2015, with the May 20 hiring of <a href="/wiki/Don_Sweeney" title="Don Sweeney">Don Sweeney</a> — long-time assistant general manager with the team. Sweeney will continue to work with current Head Coach <a href="/wiki/Claude_Julien_(ice_hockey)" title="Claude Julien (ice hockey)">Claude Julien</a>, with Cam Neely continuing as team president after only four seasons had elapsed since the Bruins' most recent Stanley Cup victory in 2011. The current administrators in the Bruins front office are:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Jacobs" title="Jeremy Jacobs">Jeremy Jacobs</a>: Owner</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Charlie_Jacobs" title="Charlie Jacobs">Charlie Jacobs</a>: Principal</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Don_Sweeney" title="Don Sweeney">Don Sweeney</a>: General Manager</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cam_Neely" title="Cam Neely">Cam Neely</a>: President<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Harry_Sinden" title="Harry Sinden">Harry Sinden</a>: Senior Advisor to the Owner</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Training_facilities">Training facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston_Bruins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Training facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Bruins previously trained and practiced at the <a href="/wiki/Bright-Landry_Hockey_Center" title="Bright-Landry Hockey Center">Bright-Landry Hockey Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Allston,_MA" class="mw-redirect" title="Allston, MA">Allston, MA</a> (built in 1956), then moved to the Ristuccia Ice Arena<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Wilmington,_MA" class="mw-redirect" title="Wilmington, MA">Wilmington, MA</a>, itself completed in 1986, before the quite recent completion of the new <a href="/wiki/Warrior_Ice_Arena" title="Warrior Ice Arena">Warrior Ice Arena</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Brighton,_Boston" title="Brighton, Boston">Brighton</a> neighborhood of Boston, where they are currently training.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Unofficial_theme_songs">Unofficial theme songs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston_Bruins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Unofficial theme songs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>When Boston television station <a href="/wiki/WSBK-TV" title="WSBK-TV">WSBK-TV</a> began broadcasting Bruins games in 1967, the producers of the games' telecasts wanted a suitable piece of music to air for the introduction of each game. Perhaps inspired by the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Ballet" title="Boston Ballet">Boston Ballet</a>'s annual Christmas performance of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Nutcracker" title="The Nutcracker">The Nutcracker</a></i> had become closely identified with Boston, <a href="/wiki/The_Ventures" title="The Ventures">The Ventures</a>' <a href="/wiki/Instrumental_rock" title="Instrumental rock">instrumental rock</a> version of the Nutcracker's overture, known as <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=MSDw3tMa7ec">"Nutty"</a>, itself thought to be that group's version of the slightly earlier hit "<a href="/wiki/Nut_Rocker" title="Nut Rocker">Nut Rocker</a>", was selected as the opening piece of music for Bruins telecasts.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> The song "Nutty" has been identified with the Bruins ever since, and is still sometimes played at the <a href="/wiki/TD_Garden" title="TD Garden">TD Garden</a> during Bruins games.</p>
<p>On ice, "Paree", a 1920s hit tune written by Leo Robin and Jose Padilla, has been played as an organ instrumental for decades, typically as the players entered the arena just before the start of each period and, for many years, after each Bruins' goal. It was introduced by <a href="/wiki/John_Kiley" title="John Kiley">John Kiley</a>, the organist for the Bruins from the 1950s through the 1980s, and is still played during Bruins' games.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Kernkraft_400" title="Kernkraft 400">Kernkraft 400</a> (Sport Chant Stadium Remix)" by <a href="/wiki/Zombie_Nation_(band)" title="Zombie Nation (band)">Zombie Nation</a> has been played for a number of seasons now <a href="/wiki/Goal_celebration#Goal_song" title="Goal celebration">after every Bruins goal scored on home ice</a>, after <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=17h4ijLjORA">two short blasts of a Kahlenberg KM-135 replica boat horn</a>. As an "influence" from its use by the Bruins, the Zombie Nation number has also been used by the Red Sox following a Sox batter's home run at Fenway Park during their most recent MLB season.</p>
<p>Currently "<a href="/wiki/Cochise_(song)" title="Cochise (song)">Cochise</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Audioslave" title="Audioslave">Audioslave</a> is played whenever the Bruins enter the ice. "<a href="/wiki/Joker_and_the_Thief" class="mw-redirect" title="Joker and the Thief">Joker and the Thief</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Wolfmother" title="Wolfmother">Wolfmother</a> is played before the opening faceoff. Conversely, after every Bruins' win at the TD Garden (as with the NESN-covered <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a> when winning a baseball game at <a href="/wiki/Fenway_Park" title="Fenway Park">Fenway Park</a>), "<a href="/wiki/Dirty_Water" title="Dirty Water">Dirty Water</a>", by <a href="/wiki/The_Standells" title="The Standells">The Standells</a>, is played.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Quincy,_Massachusetts" title="Quincy, Massachusetts">Quincy</a> <a href="/wiki/Punk_rock" title="Punk rock">punk rock</a> band <a href="/wiki/Dropkick_Murphys" title="Dropkick Murphys">Dropkick Murphys</a> wrote their song "Time to Go" (released in their 2003 album <i><a href="/wiki/Blackout_(Dropkick_Murphys_album)" title="Blackout (Dropkick Murphys album)">Blackout</a></i>) as a Bruins rally tune, and has performed <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=yOISP4xnw-Q">their own version of The Ventures' song "Nutty"</a> at games. Although it did not come with the band's guarantee to help bring home a championship, as they did with their song "<a href="/wiki/Tessie" title="Tessie">Tessie</a>" for the Red Sox, it is still a part of the team's culture and is played during third period TV timeouts. Two other <a href="/wiki/Dropkick_Murphys" title="Dropkick Murphys">Dropkick Murphys</a> songs which are sometimes played at the TD Garden to rally the home crowd are "<a href="/wiki/I%27m_Shipping_Up_to_Boston" title="I'm Shipping Up to Boston">I'm Shipping Up to Boston</a>" and "The Boys Are Back."</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bruins_Mascots">Bruins Mascots</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston_Bruins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Bruins Mascots">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Blades the Bruin,</b> an <a href="/wiki/Anthropomorphic" class="mw-redirect" title="Anthropomorphic">anthropomorphic</a> bear serves as the Bruins' team mascot. In January and February, Blades travels around the greater Boston area to raise money for the Bruins Foundation.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> For a sizable amount of the team's more recent TV and online ads, a different anthropomorphic ursine character simply known as "The Bear" appears in official Bruins video advertising.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Team_awards">Team awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston_Bruins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Team awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Bruins have several team awards that are traditionally awarded at the last home game of the regular season.</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_C._Dufresne_Trophy" class="mw-redirect" title="Elizabeth C. Dufresne Trophy">Elizabeth C. Dufresne Trophy</a><br />
<i>Best player in home games</i></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seventh_Player_Award&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Seventh Player Award (page does not exist)">Seventh Player Award</a><br />
<i>Player performing most beyond expectations</i></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eddie_Shore_Award_(Boston_Bruins)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Eddie Shore Award (Boston Bruins) (page does not exist)">Eddie Shore Award</a><br />
<i>Player with most hustle and determination</i></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_P._Bucyk_Award&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="John P. Bucyk Award (page does not exist)">John P. Bucyk Award</a><br />
<i>Community service</i></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bruins_Radio_Network_Three-Star_Awards&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bruins Radio Network Three-Star Awards (page does not exist)">Bruins Radio Network Three-Star Awards</a><br />
<i>Most three-star selections</i></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Franchise_individual_records">Franchise individual records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston_Bruins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Franchise individual records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>Most goals in a season: <a href="/wiki/Phil_Esposito" title="Phil Esposito">Phil Esposito</a>, 76 (<a href="/wiki/1970%E2%80%9371_NHL_season" title="1970–71 NHL season">1970–71</a>)</li>
<li>Most assists in a season: <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Orr" title="Bobby Orr">Bobby Orr</a>, 102 (<a href="/wiki/1970%E2%80%9371_NHL_season" title="1970–71 NHL season">1970–71</a>)</li>
<li>Most points in a season: <a href="/wiki/Phil_Esposito" title="Phil Esposito">Phil Esposito</a>, 152 (<a href="/wiki/1970%E2%80%9371_NHL_season" title="1970–71 NHL season">1970–71</a>)</li>
<li>Most penalty minutes in a season: <a href="/wiki/Jay_Miller_(ice_hockey)" title="Jay Miller (ice hockey)">Jay Miller</a>, 304 (<a href="/wiki/1987%E2%80%9388_NHL_season" title="1987–88 NHL season">1987–88</a>)</li>
<li>Lowest goals against average in a season: <a href="/wiki/Frank_Brimsek" title="Frank Brimsek">Frank Brimsek</a>, 1.56, (<a href="/wiki/1938%E2%80%9339_NHL_season" title="1938–39 NHL season">1938–39</a>)</li>
<li>Most points per game in a season: <a href="/wiki/Bill_Cowley" title="Bill Cowley">Bill Cowley</a>, 1.97 (<a href="/wiki/1943%E2%80%9344_NHL_season" title="1943–44 NHL season">1943–44</a>)</li>
<li>Most points in a season, defenseman: <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Orr" title="Bobby Orr">Bobby Orr</a>, 139 (<a href="/wiki/1970%E2%80%9371_NHL_season" title="1970–71 NHL season">1970–71</a>)</li>
<li>Most points in a season, rookie: <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A9_Juneau" title="Joé Juneau">Joe Juneau</a>, 102 (<a href="/wiki/1992%E2%80%9393_NHL_season" title="1992–93 NHL season">1992–93</a>)</li>
<li>Most wins in a season: <a href="/wiki/Pete_Peeters" title="Pete Peeters">Pete Peeters</a>, 40 (<a href="/wiki/1982%E2%80%9383_NHL_season" title="1982–83 NHL season">1982–83</a>)</li>
<li>Most shutouts in a season: <a href="/wiki/Hal_Winkler" title="Hal Winkler">Hal Winkler</a>, 15 (<a href="/wiki/1927%E2%80%9328_NHL_season" title="1927–28 NHL season">1927–28</a>)</li>
<li>Consecutive games streak: <a href="/wiki/John_Bucyk" class="mw-redirect" title="John Bucyk">John Bucyk</a>, 418 (January 23, 1969 – March 2, 1975)</li>
<li>Longest point scoring streak: <a href="/wiki/Bronco_Horvath" title="Bronco Horvath">Bronco Horvath</a>, 22 games, (<a href="/wiki/1959%E2%80%9360_NHL_season" title="1959–60 NHL season">1959–60</a>)</li>
<li>Highest save percentage in a season: <a href="/wiki/Tim_Thomas_(ice_hockey)" title="Tim Thomas (ice hockey)">Tim Thomas</a>, .938 (<a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_NHL_season" title="2010–11 NHL season">2010–11</a>)</li>
<li>Longest winning streak by a goaltender, one season: Gilles Gilbert, 17 (1975–76)</li>
</ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="General_managers">General managers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston_Bruins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: General managers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">For more details on this topic, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_Boston_Bruins_general_managers" title="List of Boston Bruins general managers">List of Boston Bruins general managers</a>.</div>
<p>Following the team's failure to make the 2015 playoffs, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Chiarelli_(ice_hockey)" title="Peter Chiarelli (ice hockey)">Peter Chiarelli</a> was fired as General Manager on April 15, 2015, with <a href="/wiki/Don_Sweeney" title="Don Sweeney">Don Sweeney</a> hired as Chiarelli's replacement on May 20, 2015.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Head_coaches">Head coaches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston_Bruins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Head coaches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">For more details on this topic, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_Boston_Bruins_head_coaches" title="List of Boston Bruins head coaches">List of Boston Bruins head coaches</a>.</div>
<p>The current head coach is <a href="/wiki/Claude_Julien_(ice_hockey)" title="Claude Julien (ice hockey)">Claude Julien</a>, who was hired on June 22, 2007, guiding the Bruins to <a href="/wiki/2011_Stanley_Cup_Finals" title="2011 Stanley Cup Finals">their sixth Stanley Cup championship in 2011</a>. Before the Stanley Cup victory, at the conclusion of the <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_NHL_season#Awards" title="2008–09 NHL season">2008–09 NHL season</a>, Julien was awarded the Jack Adams Award as the best coach in the NHL. More recently, during a six-game roadtrip for the Bruins as part of the team's <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Boston_Bruins_season" title="2015–16 Boston Bruins season">2015–16 season</a>, on February 13, 2016 Julien was surprised to learn, after his Bruins team defeated the <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Wild" title="Minnesota Wild">Minnesota Wild</a> in a 4-2 road victory, that he had coached his 500th NHL winning game.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> On March 3, 2016, as the result of Julien's coaching the Bruins to a 4-2 home ice win against the 2015 Stanley Cup champion Chicago Blackhawks, Julien's winning game total as the Bruins' head coach rose to 387 wins for the Boston team, equalling the total number of Bruins coaching wins for Hall of Fame member <a href="/wiki/Art_Ross" title="Art Ross">Art Ross</a>, the Bruins' original coach in 1924, from their beginnings that year through <a href="/wiki/List_of_Boston_Bruins_head_coaches#Coaches" title="List of Boston Bruins head coaches">four separated periods of coaching</a> ending in 1939.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
